<a id="t-91c6c489cb"></a>
## Thread: Why GOBACK? — 5 msgs

### Why GOBACK?

- **From:** walterm@hprctbs3.rose.hp.com (Walter Murray)
- **Date:** 1994-12-12T15:18:27+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3chpk3$ln9@hpchase.rose.hp.com>`

```
Several recent articles have advocated use of the GOBACK statement.
GOBACK is not Standard COBOL.  Is it an IBM thing?  What are the
advantages of using it, as opposed to STOP RUN or EXIT PROGRAM?

Walter
```

#### ↳ Re: Why GOBACK?

- **From:** wcivy@adpc.purdue.edu
- **Date:** 1994-12-12T16:32:54-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3cihgk$mej@mozo.cc.purdue.edu>`
- **References:** `<3chpk3$ln9@hpchase.rose.hp.com>`

```

In article <3chpk3$ln9@hpchase.rose.hp.com>, <walterm@hprctbs3.rose.hp.com> 
writes:
> Several recent articles have advocated use of the GOBACK statement.
> GOBACK is not Standard COBOL.  Is it an IBM thing?  What are the
> advantages of using it, as opposed to STOP RUN or EXIT PROGRAM?
> 
> Walter

It might be an IBM thing - I've got the IBM OS/VS COBOL manual, and it lists 
all three (EXIT PROGRAM, STOP RUN, and GOBACK).

The manual says the EXIT PROGRAM statement is "Nonoperational" (!?) if placed 
in a "Main Program", one which is directly started by the operating system (as 
opposed to being started by being CALLed by another COBOL program).

The two we have always used are STOP RUN and GOBACK.  Both will end your 
program and return to the operating system, if the program is a "Main Program". 
If your program is a "Subprogram", started with a CALL from another COBOL 
program, a GOBACK will exit your program and return to the CALLing program, 
where a STOP RUN will **completely end this program and the entire set of 
programs that are running, returning you to the operating system**!!

This probably isn't what you want in a Subprogram.  :-)

This means that GOBACK works to end your program and return to either the 
operating system or to the CALLing program, whether your program is being run 
as a Main Program or as a Subprogram.  

So, GOBACK works in *every* instance to end this program, where STOP RUN only 
gives you what you want some of the time.

Q) Don't you know know whether a program is a Main Program or a Subprogram?

A) All of them can be Subprograms (at least on IBM mainframe -- I haven't tried 
this on other platforms).  You can take COBOL programs you wrote, intending to 
run them as Main Programs, and write a supervising COBOL program that runs (by 
CALLing) them in the appropriate sequence.  Without having to recompile them or 
change them in any way.  You do have to plan ahead, so that the file 
identifiers work together, so that files written are then read by the correct 
program.  On our mainframe, we specify the same "DD" name in the "SELECT 
file-name, ASSIGN TO ddname" statement.

I haven't run across many real applications for this, but one was back in the 
olden days when we still wrote bunches of report programs for systems (now we 
just give them access to the file and SAS or RAMIS reporting programs!).  Many 
of the report programs for this system reported the same data, just in 
different sequences, with different control breaks and sub-totals, and so on. 
Naturally, the same format wouldn't work, so we had 12-15 report programs that 
the customer could request 'nn' copies of any of the reports at any time.  We 
wrote a control program that ran the report programs.  It did this based on a 
control file that consisted of the report program name and the number of copies 
of the report desired.  This way, instead of having to have a variety of job 
setups for the different reports, we had one job setup that you fed control 
cards to.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Why GOBACK?

- **From:** Richard_Plinston@kcbbs.gen.nz (Richard Plinston)
- **Date:** 1994-12-13T19:37:17+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3294346.70637.17776@kcbbs.gen.nz>`
- **References:** `<3cihgk$mej@mozo.cc.purdue.edu>`

```
>
>The manual says the EXIT PROGRAM statement is "Nonoperational" (!?) if placed  
…[11 more quoted lines elided]…
>
All it needs is:

          EXIT PROGRAM
          STOP RUN
          .

This works in all situations, and is probably what GOBACK expands to.
(and it's real COBOL   ;-)

Hope this helps
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Why GOBACK?

- **From:** Don Nelson <nelson_don@tandem.com>
- **Date:** 1994-12-15T18:57:59+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<D0v8op.2pI@tandem.com>`
- **References:** `<3294346.70637.17776@kcbbs.gen.nz>`

```
In article <3294346.70637.17776@kcbbs.gen.nz> Richard Plinston,
Richard_Plinston@kcbbs.gen.nz writes:
>>
>>The manual says the EXIT PROGRAM statement is "Nonoperational" (!?) if
placed  
>>in a "Main Program", one which is directly started by the operating
system (as  
>>opposed to being started by being CALLed by another COBOL program).
>>
>>The two we have always used are STOP RUN and GOBACK.  Both will end
your  
>>program and return to the operating system, if the program is a "Main
Program".  
>>If your program is a "Subprogram", started with a CALL from another
COBOL  
>>program, a GOBACK will exit your program and return to the CALLing
program,  
>>where a STOP RUN will **completely end this program and the entire set
of  
>>programs that are running, returning you to the operating system**!!
>>
…[9 more quoted lines elided]…
>(and it's real COBOL   ;-)
I hoped to stay out of this, but there is so much misinformation 
going around that I thought I ought to state the facts.  First, as 
has been stated many times, GOBACK is not in the standard and is not 
likely to be added to the standard (it has never been seriously 
proposed to the standards groups, and most of the members feel it is 
rather grotesque).  It originated as an IBM extension a long time 
ago, and exists in lots of compilers (not mine, however).  According 
to the standard, EXIT PROGRAM is a no-op if it is specified in a main 
program.  Somebody said their compiler did not accept EXIT PROGRAM, 
so that compiler obviously does not conform to the standard.  STOP 
RUN stops the run unit or whatever you want to call it.  
Unfortunately, the simple expedient of EXIT PROGRAM immediately 
followed by STOP RUN is an illegal combination according to the 
standard.  The standard says that EXIT PROGRAM must be the last thing 
in a sentence (most compilers don't enforce this rule).  This means 
you have to put a period after the EXIT PROGRAM in the example above, 
which precludes it from being used in a delimited scope statement (IF 
... END-IF for example).  In the next standard, the period will not 
be required, so there is probably no reason to add GOBACK other than 
it avoids three additional words.

Don Nelson
COBOL Development, Tandem Computers, Inc.
Member, ANSI X3J4 and ISO/IEC JTC1/SC22 WG4 COBOL Committees
Project Editor, 1997 ISO COBOL Standard
Moderator, COBOL Conference, Bix
nelson_don@tandem.com
donn@bix.com
No clever quotes here
```

#### ↳ Re: Why GOBACK?

- **From:** pahint@eunet.be (Pieter Hintjens)
- **Date:** 1994-12-13T17:43:31+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<D0rFwK.D6w@Belgium.EU.net>`
- **References:** `<3chpk3$ln9@hpchase.rose.hp.com>`

```
Walter Murray (walterm@hprctbs3.rose.hp.com) wrote:
: Several recent articles have advocated use of the GOBACK statement.
: GOBACK is not Standard COBOL.  Is it an IBM thing?  What are the
: advantages of using it, as opposed to STOP RUN or EXIT PROGRAM?

: Walter

As far as I know, GOBACK is a workaround for the fact that EXIT
PROGRAM does not work in main programs.  You need to use STOP RUN
instead, and obviously someone complained that this was a pain.
Use GOBACK and your program returns to the caller, be it another
COBOL program, or the system.

There is, however, another way to do this, which is to structure
your program so that the EXIT PROGRAM paragraph is followed by a
paragraph containing STOP RUN.  If the EXIT PROGRAM 'fails', ie.
your program was run as a main, the STOP RUN will hit.  This is
more portable than using GOBACK, since the same problem will
hit you on other systems, where STOP RUN is also mandatory.  I
think this is the case for Micro-Focus (Unix).
```

---

```
I have some (I kept them for historical reasons - basically, I am a 
pack rat).  However, these forms were designed for programmers to 
code on and then turn into keypunch to get punched.  I would think 
that nobody uses keypunches today.  Even without tools, I assume that

are of little use in this situation.  It is easier to write out the 
program on paper and then type it in if you are going to use paper.  
Writing in the little boxes on forms is lots harder.

I even have report layout sheets.  They might be of marginal use.

If you want any of this, let me know (along with your address) and I 
can send a couple of each.  You would have to photocopy them.
```

## Thread: COBOL650 where is the linker — 7 msgs

### COBOL650 where is the linker

- **From:** nelson@turing.uncg.edu (Michael Nelson)
- **Date:** 1994-12-12T21:38:33+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3cifsp$dsa@bruce.uncg.edu>`

```
For some reason the file COBOL650.ZIP that I downloaded does not have a 
linker.  Do I need one...I would quess so, but I don't have it......anyone
have any ideas?
```

```
the linker was able to run on DOS & OS/2 along (in 16 bit-mode of course).
```

```
As part of the research for an ongoing project I would like to
ask for your input by completing the following survey. Please
forward a copy to your friends and/or co-workers for the purpose
outlined in the copyright section.

The objective of the survey is to determine
    - what programming tools are currently in use
    - whether their use improves productivity
    - whether there is room for improvement

If you are a programmer by profession I strongly urge you to
please take part. There are a total of 15 questions. It should
only take 10 to 15 minutes of your time.

survey will be released.

    ac456@freenet.carleton.ca

participation.

of collecting data.
```

## Thread: COBOL and Linux — 2 msgs

### COBOL and Linux

- **From:** M.Turk@uws.EDU.AU (Michael Turk)
- **Date:** 1994-12-14T12:25:13
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<M.Turk.196.000C6BF7@uws.EDU.AU>`

```
Just adding my 2 cents worth.
I think a version of COBOL 85 that runs under Linux would be a good idea!
There are heaps of students who cannot afford commercial versions of COBOL 
around.  Many of my students run GNU C, C++ and Ada - a GNU COBOL would be 
most welcome!

Michael


Michael Turk
m.turk@uws.edu.au

University of Western Sydney, Macarthur
Visit Camden, at the rural edge of Sydney, Australia
```

#### ↳ Re: COBOL and Linux

- **From:** dewar@cs.nyu.edu (Robert Dewar)
- **Date:** 1994-12-15T07:52:42-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3cpe6q$94o@gnat.cs.nyu.edu>`
- **References:** `<M.Turk.196.000C6BF7@uws.EDU.AU>`

```
Michael, just so you don't get a wrong impression, I absolutely agree that
a GNU-COBOL would be great to have. My reservations are not based on the
desirability of such a product, but rather on the knowledge that to do a
reasonably complete job is a big project -- I would estimate a minimum of
four person years of very knowledgable people working on such a project
full time.

Now of course by subsetting COBOL, you can make the project arbitrarily
easier, but the question is how big does the subset have to be to be useful.

I am sure incidentally that a GNU-COBOL is MUCH easier to do than a
COBOL to C translator, since GCC provides a much richer environment at
the level of the GCC tree than C.

It is true that doing a GCC COBOL would require more extensive initial
knowledge, but that's a relatively minor hurdle in the long run.
```

---

## Thread: Micro Focus SQL Pre-compiler — 2 msgs

_Topics: [`Compilers and vendors`](topics.md#compilers) · [`Databases and SQL`](topics.md#databases)_

### Micro Focus SQL Pre-compiler

- **From:** keng@infinet.com (Kenneth M. Good)
- **Date:** 1994-12-14T16:27:23+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3cn6db$mbl@rigel.infinet.com>`

```
I would like to use our Teradata DBC/1012 SQL data base computer in our PC 
environment.  Currently all of our development work is done on the PC 
with the exception of programs which contain imbedded-SQL.  Our CODASYL 
data base is emulated, this allows us to compile and test mainframe 
programs.  This test procedure falls apart when a program with 
imbedded-SQL is encountered.  Our perferred direction would be to access 
the DBC/1012 computer directly for our testing.  We have the API provided 
by Teradata (Now AT&T GIS), but I don't wish to write a pre-compiler for 
imbedded-SQL.  How do I get a Teradata DBC/1012 SQL pre-compiler for 
Micro Focus COBOL.  If one is not available, does anyone have source code 
for a SQL pre-compiler.  This would make my life easier.
```

#### ↳ Re: Micro Focus SQL Pre-compiler

- **From:** Alan Wheeler <71333.2247@CompuServe.COM>
- **Date:** 1994-12-15T17:22:12+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3cpu04$9ct$2@mhadg.production.compuserve.com>`
- **References:** `<3cn6db$mbl@rigel.infinet.com>`

```
To my knowledge, there is no commercially available SQL 
precompiler for the Teradata database for use with Micro Focus 
COBOL.  There are a number of other SQL precompilers available, 
from IBM's DB2/2, to MS SQL Server, to Sybase, Oracle, Informix, 
Ingress, XDB, and maybe a few others.  If none of those will 
offer you reasonable compatability to the Teradata database, or 
embedded SQL code, then you could use the Micro Focus 
Preprocessor facility, which is part of their Workbench product, 
to write what ever precompiler that you want.

Regards, Alan.
```

## Thread: Help, please — 2 msgs

_Topics: [`Help requests and how-to`](topics.md#help)_

### Re: Help, please

- **From:** tbs@iii1.iii.net (Tony B. Shepherd)
- **Date:** 1994-12-14T13:57:48-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3cnf7v$ri4@iii1.iii.net>`
- **References:** `<D03DLr.CA7@bfsec.bt.co.uk> <3bj9a9$mv8@freenet.vancouver.bc.ca>`

```
}In article <3bj9a9$mv8@freenet.vancouver.bc.ca>,
}Ron Ross <bcdiver@freenet.vancouver.bc.ca> wrote:
}>PaulGordon wrote:
}>: Could anyone think of a solution to this problem . 
}>: I have a six bit field  that is passed to me as a variable with 
}>: a PICTURE clause of PIC X. I want to convert this six 
}>: bit field into a 2 digit number ( 2^6 = 64 so it can't be bigger
}>: than two digits). How would this be done ?
}>       01  WS-ALPHA FIELD.
}>           05  FILLER             PIC 9      VALUE ZERO.
  make it:   05  FILLER             PIC X   VALUE LOW-VALUE.
  why? on HP3000 (Ascii) just 'PIC 9' gives zoned decimal format,
   and VALUE ZERO gives x'30' (decimal 48).
}>           05  WS-PASSED-FIELD    PIC X.
}>
}>       01  WS-NUMERIC-FIELD       REDEFINES  WS-ALPHA-FIELD
}>                                  PIC 9(02)  BINARY.
}>    The "BINARY" claues is the ANSI 85 standard, depending on your
}>machine/compiler it could be "COMP" or "COMP-4".

And now for a trickier question: how can one tell if the program is 
executing on an Ascii or Ebcdic machine at execution time?

Tony B. Shepherd  --  tbs@iii.net  --  Happy Holidays
```

#### ↳ Re: Help, please

- **From:** pahint@eunet.be (Pieter Hintjens)
- **Date:** 1994-12-15T07:40:28+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<D0uDBG.MK3@Belgium.EU.net>`
- **References:** `<D03DLr.CA7@bfsec.bt.co.uk> <3bj9a9$mv8@freenet.vancouver.bc.ca> <3cnf7v$ri4@iii1.iii.net>`

```
Tony B. Shepherd (tbs@iii1.iii.net) wrote:
: And now for a trickier question: how can one tell if the program is 
: executing on an Ascii or Ebcdic machine at execution time?

Under ASCII, "0" has value 48, while "A" has value 65.  Under EBCDIC,
"0" has value 240, while "A" has value 193. So just compare:

    02  CHARACTER-0       PIC X   VALUE "0".

    IF CHARACTER-0 < "A"
        we are on an ASCII system
    ELSE
        we are on an EBCDIC system
    .
```

---

<a id="t-49eb5c556d"></a>
## Thread: Does Micro Focus have good tools? — 3 msgs

_Topics: [`Compilers and vendors`](topics.md#compilers)_

### Does Micro Focus have good tools?

- **From:** abdu@agora.rdrop.com (Abdel-Hadi Bukres)
- **Date:** 1994-12-15T04:06:05+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<D0u3E6.Ly0@agora.rdrop.com>`

```

I am using Wang's COBOL compiler and we have tools for screen formatting.
I use a tool called EZFORMAT where I can put all of a screen's text and
fields on the screen and EZFORMAT would generate a COBOL section that 
can be inserted into my program. WANG's COBOL also have a display and
read function that can display a whole screen, does data verification and
gets user input using one single function.

My question here is does Micor Focus have similat tools and what's the
name of the tool/program that is similar to our EZFORMAT?

Abdu
```

#### ↳ Re: Does Micro Focus have good tools?

- **From:** Alan Wheeler <71333.2247@CompuServe.COM>
- **Date:** 1994-12-15T17:15:52+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3cptk8$9ct$1@mhadg.production.compuserve.com>`
- **References:** `<D0u3E6.Ly0@agora.rdrop.com>`

```
Yes, the Micro Focus compiler includes a similar tool, called 
SCREENS, which will allow you to paint your screens and generate 
the COBOL code necessary to use them.  There are, also, third 
party services & packages available to convert Wang applications 
to Micro Focus applications or to emulate some of the key Wang 
facilities on the PC, in conjunction with a Micro Focus comiled 
application.  If you have access to the Micro Focus Forum on 
CompuServe, these are listed in one of the Library files, whose 
search keyword is WANG.  If you are interested and you don't have 
 access to CompuServe, let me know and I will forward a copy of 
the information.

Regards, Alan.
```

## Thread: Legacy systems - Mainframe to Unix — 1 msgs

_Topics: [`COBOL's future, legacy, and obsolescence`](topics.md#future) · [`Mainframe, z/OS, JCL, CICS`](topics.md#mainframe)_

### Legacy systems - Mainframe to Unix

- **From:** Sol@barron.demon.co.uk (Sol Barron)
- **Date:** 1994-12-15T07:59:50+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<787478390snz@barron.demon.co.uk>`

```
Hi,

Can anyone tell me which newsgroup this should be posted to. I'm trying to 
contact mainframe (IBM, ICL, etc.) users with Cobol-based systems who would
like to migrate to Unix but can't.

My company offers a service through a proprietary toolset which automatically
converts mainframe Cobol hierarchical database or flat file systems to 
relational systems on Unix. In the process we remove the need for a monitor
(such as CICS) and the end product requires no further licencing other than 
the RDBMS. The process is automated, involves no rewriting or re-engineering
and is completed within three to six months. 

The customer gets a system, functionally identical to the old one (warts
all!) and places the customer in a position where they can further develop any
parts of the system they feel can make better use of the RDBMS, SQL, client
server, etc.

So far we've done a couple of migrations here in the UK and I'm looking to
cast the net further afield. If anyone is interested or knows the best forum
for this, please let me know.

Thanks
```

## Thread: MF COBOL for AIX: ADD-Error — 3 msgs

_Topics: [`Compilers and vendors`](topics.md#compilers)_

### MF COBOL for AIX: ADD-Error

- **From:** cal@zls.gtn.com (C. A. Lademann)
- **Date:** 1994-12-15T15:08:42+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1994Dec15.150842.1412@zls.gtn.com>`

```
Hi, folks.
Take a look at the following small program that reproduces an error
with computational-arithmetics using Micro Focus COBOL for AIX on 
IBM RS/6000 (even worse than the Pentium-FDIV-error, this one occurs
every 28 seconds :-)):

       IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
       PROGRAM-ID. jtest.
       ENVIRONMENT DIVISION.
       CONFIGURATION SECTION.
       OBJECT-COMPUTER. ALTOS.
       SPECIAL-NAMES.
       INPUT-OUTPUT SECTION.

       WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
       01 J1        PIC 9(3)V9(2) comp.
       01 J3        PIC 9(3).9(2).

       PROCEDURE DIVISION.
       move 15 to J1.
       add 100 to J1.
       move J1 to J3.
       display J3 at 0101.

       stop run.

Instead of the expected value of 115, J3 contains the value 16!!!

Using the compiler-directive "IBMCOMP" avoids the calculation-error,
but also increases the size of the comp-data-elements.

So, what can I do? Does anybody else have this or similar problems?
Even Micro Focus, Newbury, UK could not answer that question.

Please, post or mail to <cal@zls.gtn.com>.
```

<a id="t-c143382723"></a>
## Thread: Help, please — 1 msgs

_Topics: [`Help requests and how-to`](topics.md#help)_

### Re: Help, please

- **From:** tbs@iii1.iii.net (Tony B. Shepherd)
- **Date:** 1994-12-15T12:37:16-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3cpusv$oj9@iii1.iii.net>`
- **References:** `<D03DLr.CA7@bfsec.bt.co.uk> <3bj9a9$mv8@freenet.vancouver.bc.ca> <3cnf7v$ri4@iii1.iii.net> <D0uDBG.MK3@belgium.eu.net>`

```
In article <D0uDBG.MK3@belgium.eu.net>,
Pieter Hintjens <pahint@eunet.be> wrote:
>Tony B. Shepherd (tbs@iii1.iii.net) wrote:
>: And now for a trickier question: how can one tell if the program is 
…[9 more quoted lines elided]…
>        we are on an EBCDIC system

GREAT!!!!  Many people know that Ebcdic '0' > Ebcdic 'A' (as well as
Ebcdic 'a' < Ebcdic 'A'), but you would be surprised how many people
give the answer as:
     IF "0" < "A"
       etc.

Of course that won't work (and there is the trick).

My congratulations Pieter!

In the same vein, those who face conversion from one-character binary to 
hexadecimal or other such games might consider a different approach.  
Construct a table (at execution time or compile time) of the answers, and 
use (incoming value + 1) as a subscript.  For examples, the table for hex 
conversion would look like:
     01  HEX-VALUES.
       03  PIC X(32) VALUE "000102030405060708090A0B0C0D0E0F".
       ...
       03  PIC X(32) VALUE "F0F1F2F3F4F5F6F7F8F9FAFBFCFDFEFF".
     01  REDEFINES HEX-VALUES.
       03  HEX-VALUE PIC XX OCCURS 256 TIMES.

I have used this method quite successfully in several instances, 
including translating 7-bit no parity Ascii to 8-bit Ascii, with 
Even/Odd/No parity specified at execution time.  In another case it was
much easier to break bytes to nybbles for packed no-sign decimal (two 
digits per byte, no sign nybble).

Regards, and best holiday wishes.  Back to the shadows - Tony B. Shepherd
```

---

<a id="t-72f1aeae91"></a>
## Thread: posting cobol tutorial possibilites. — 2 msgs

_Topics: [`Tutorials, books, learning`](topics.md#learning)_

### posting cobol tutorial possibilites.

- **From:** 6848830@LMSC5.IS.LMSC.LOCKHEED.COM
- **Date:** 1994-12-15T17:01:34-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1708DEF6ES86.6848830@LMSC5.IS.LMSC.LOCKHEED.COM>`

```
Hello:
I have some questions about the internet, specifically comp.lang.cobol.
If a person starts posting small sections of a cobol tutorial on the
cobol subject, do they lose the copyright once it is on the internet?
 
Also, if a person gets source code with Micro Focus COBOL and then
changes it, do they violate copyright of Micro Focus?
 
I would like to start posting some tutorials I am working on.  But I
don't know about the legal ramifications.
 
I know Micro Focus people read this newsgroup, and I wonder how they
would feel if I posted a revised version of their program winhello.cbl.
 
I would like to add on to winhello.cbl in increments and post the
changes, to demonstrate various Windows programming techniques.
 
I would like to post an example of winhello.cbl that goes beyond
just calling DrawText and displaying "Hello World".  I would like
to show a COBOL program using Dialog Boxes and Icons and
Menus.  So far I have been able to get it to read, write and
so forth to an isam file.
 
In order to do this, do I have to pay royalties to the original
copyright owner (Micro Focus)?
 
Since I am a man of modest means, what can I do to avoid this?
Compromise?  Do I have to code the Message loop from scratch without
using Winhello.cbl as a base?
 
My other internet i.d. is chrism@saigon.com
 
I don't want to cause any trouble.
 
regards,
 
Chris Mason
"The Unknown COBOL Programmer"
The opinions expressed are mine, not my Employers.
      6848830@lmsc5.is.lmsc.lockheed.com
LMSC5:  Tons of Beautiful Big Blue Iron...
```

#### ↳ Re: posting cobol tutorial possibilites.

- **From:** jfid@mfltd.co.uk (James Fidell)
- **Date:** 1994-12-16T14:43:21
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3cs929$ijk@icebox.mfltd.co.uk>`
- **References:** `<1708DEF6ES86.6848830@LMSC5.IS.LMSC.LOCKHEED.COM>`

```

In article <1708DEF6ES86.6848830@LMSC5.IS.LMSC.LOCKHEED.COM>, 6848830@LMSC5.IS.LMSC.LOCKHEED.COM writes:
> Hello:
> I have some questions about the internet, specifically comp.lang.cobol.
> If a person starts posting small sections of a cobol tutorial on the
> cobol subject, do they lose the copyright once it is on the internet?

I'm no expert on this, but what follows is my understanding of the situation
based on discussions between many of the FAQ maintainers.

The Berne Convention guarantees you copyright of any work and you would
retain that should you post it on USENET or make it available some other
way on the Internet.  However, should you wish to be able to sue for
lost income due to someone infringing your copyright, I believe that many
places require that you register a copyright.

> Also, if a person gets source code with Micro Focus COBOL and then
> changes it, do they violate copyright of Micro Focus?

I don't believe that changing the code would, but publishing the changed
code might.

> I would like to start posting some tutorials I am working on.  But I
> don't know about the legal ramifications.

Should you do so, perhaps you'd like to put them on the Micro Focus FTP
server too ?

> I know Micro Focus people read this newsgroup, and I wonder how they
> would feel if I posted a revised version of their program winhello.cbl.

Personally, I don't see why there would be a problem with this, but I'll
try to get a definitive position for you.

> In order to do this, do I have to pay royalties to the original
> copyright owner (Micro Focus)?

Because <a body> holds copyright on something doesn't mean that you
would *have* to pay royalties for using it.  The body in question may
ask for royalties or they may allow you to use the code freely as long
as you make no profit by it.  As I said, I will try to find someone who
can give you a definitive position for this.

> Since I am a man of modest means, what can I do to avoid this?
> Compromise?  Do I have to code the Message loop from scratch without
> using Winhello.cbl as a base?

There is a copyright FAQ which you might like to read for more information.
I don't know where it appears, but it's certain to be available for
anonymous FTP on rtfm.mit.edu in /pub/usenet-by-...

James.
```

## Thread: C programmer seeks COBOL wisdom — 1 msgs

### C programmer seeks COBOL wisdom

- **From:** tcj@infoseek.com (Todd Jonz)

```
I can remember answering this question myself countless numbers of times many
moons ago, but today it seems that everything I once knew about COBOL has
slipped through the holes in my Swiss cheese brain.

I am writing a program that will read ASCII files produced by a COBOL program,
but *my* program is *not* written in COBOL.  My input files contain signed
numerics that would be defined in COBOL as "PIC S9(n)V99" and that look like
"000000{".  I recall that COBOL munges the last byte of such values to store
the sign (e.g. if I recall correctly, the value above represents a "positive
zero"), but I can't for the life of me remember the algorithm used to do this
munging.  Can someone please refresh my faulty memory?  Tnx in advance,


							-- Todd
```
